Parsing the Phrase 'Wa l-Ḥaml' in the Matn
Author provides grammatical analysis of 'wa l-ḥaml'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two grammatical readings of the phrase 'wa l-ḥaml' as explained in the commentary.

Core Idea
The same phrase can be read in two ways: hyperbole or substitution of an absolute object.

The commentator here provides a grammatical note on the matn's phrase 'wa l-ḥaml'. Understanding the parsing of this phrase is essential to correctly interpret the logical point being made. This lesson will walk you through the two grammatical possibilities and their implications.

Guided Path
1
Locate the phrase in the Arabic
Find the phrase 'wa l-ḥaml' (وَالْحَمْل) in the matn. Notice it is the subject of the commentator's analysis.
2
Identify the first reading: hyperbolic predication
The first possibility is that the phrase is a hyperbolic predication (mubālagha), like saying 'Zayd is justice' to mean Zayd is very just. Here, 'the ultimate approximation of the goal' is directly predicated onto 'this' in a hyperbolic sense.
This reading treats the grammar as straightforward predication with an exaggerated meaning.
3
Identify the second reading: absolute object substituting for predicate
The second possibility is that the predicate of the subject is omitted, and 'the ultimate approximation of the goal' is an absolute object (mafʿūl muṭlaq) that has taken the place of the predicate. This causes it to be raised to the nominative case (rafʿ) from its original accusative.
The implied meaning is 'This speech approximates the utmost approximation.'
4
Recognize the parallel with an earlier phrase
The commentator notes a similar instance earlier in the matn: 'So this is the ultimate refinement of speech.' This reinforces the pattern of using an absolute object in place of a predicate.
Understanding this pattern helps in reading other similar constructions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۰۸) قوله و الحمل اى حمل قوله غاية تقريب المرام على كلمة اسم الاشارة هذا اما على طريقة المبالغة كما يقال فى حمل المصادر على الذوات نحو زيد «عدل او ان خبر المبتداء محذوف و غاية تقريب» «المرام» مفعول مطلق اقيم مقامه فاعطى حكمه وهو الرفع على الخبرية بعد ما كان منصوباً على المفعولية والتقدير: هذا الكلام مقرب غاية التقريب وقد تقدم مثله في قوله: فهذا غاية تهذيب الكلام». (التقريب ص ۱۱)
(108) His words 'and the predication' i.e., the predication of his words 'the ultimate approximation of the goal' upon the word of the demonstrative pronoun 'this'. This is either by way of hyperbole, as it is said in the predication of sources onto essences like 'Zayd is justice' or that the predicate of the subject is omitted and 'the ultimate approximation of the goal' is an absolute object that took its place, so it was given its ruling, which is nominative as a predicate after it was accusative as an object, and the estimation is: 'This speech approximates the utmost approximation.' A similar instance has preceded in his words: 'So this is the ultimate refinement of speech.' (al-Taqrīb p. 11)
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage is a parsing exercise on the phrase 'wa l-ḥaml' (and the predication) in the matn. The commentator explains that it refers to the act of predicating the phrase 'the ultimate approximation of the goal' (ghāyat taqrīb al-marām) upon the demonstrative word 'this' (hādhā). He gives two grammatical analyses. First, it can be treated as a hyperbolic predication (ṭarīqat al-mubālagha), like saying 'Zayd is justice' meaning Zayd is very just. Second, it can be that the predicate of the subject is omitted, and 'the ultimate approximation of the goal' is an absolute object (mafʿūl muṭlaq) that has taken the place of the predicate, thus becoming nominative (rafʿ) in subject position, whereas normally it would be accusative. The implied meaning is 'This speech approximates the utmost approximation.' He notes that a similar instance occurred earlier in the matn: 'So this is the ultimate refinement of speech.' This passage is a technical grammatical note that aids in reading the text correctly.

مبالغة

Key Takeaway
The parsing of 'wa l-ḥaml' reveals two possible readings: hyperbolic predication or an absolute object substituting for a predicate; the commentator favors the latter as the implicit meaning.

The Particle 'Min' as Generic Specification in Arabic Grammar
Author clarifies 'min' as generic specification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether 'min' is functioning as generic (bayān al-jins) or partitive (tab‘īḍ) in Quranic and scholarly Arabic passages.

Core Idea
The particle 'min' can specify the genus, not just partitive—a key distinction for precise parsing of Islamic texts.

In Arabic grammar, the particle 'min' has multiple functions. One debated use is bayān al-jins, which specifies the category or kind of something, as opposed to partitive which indicates a part of a whole. This hashia clarifies that the matn's use of 'min' is indeed generic, citing Quranic evidence. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly interpreting Islamic legal and theological phrases.

Guided Path
1
Locate the 'min' phrase
Find the phrase 'min taqrīr ʿaqāʾid al-Islām' in the passage. What exactly follows 'min'?
This phrase is the focus of the commentary.
2
Identify the grammatical claim
The commentator explicitly says 'min' is for bayān al-jins (clarifying the genus). Note the Quranic examples he provides to support this usage.
The examples are 'Mā nansakh min āya' and 'Fajtanibū l-rijsa mina l-awthān'.
3
Consider the counterargument
Some scholars deny generic 'min' and insist it is always partitive (tab‘īḍ). Think about how the meaning would change if 'min' were partitive instead of generic in the given phrase.
Partitive would imply 'some of the affirmation' versus generic 'the category of affirmation'.
4
Apply to a real example
Apply the distinction to the Quranic verse 'Fajtanibū l-rijsa mina l-awthān' (22:30). Test both interpretations: generic (avoid the category of idol-abomination) vs. partitive (avoid some of the idol-abomination). Which seems correct?
Context usually supports generic here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۱۰) يعنى ان كلمة «من» لبيان الجنس فان هذه و ان كان اكثر وقوعها بعدما و مهما لكثرة ابها مهما نحو: «ما ننسخ من آية ...» ، «مهما تأتنا به من آية» لكنها قديحي بعد غير هما ايضاً قال تعالى: «فاجتنبوا الرجس من الاوثان ثم هى و مخفوضها في محل النصب على الحالية اى كائناً من تقرير عقايد الاسلام وكذا الحال فى امثال ذلك. ثم ان قوماً انكر مجى ( من البيان الجنس وعليه فهى للتبعيض كما لا يخفى. (محمد على)
(110) It means that the word 'min' is for clarifying the genus. Although it occurs most often after 'mā' and 'mahmā' due to their frequent ambiguity, like 'What verse We abrogate...', 'Whatever sign you bring us', it may also come after other words. Allah says: 'So avoid the abomination of idols.' Then it and its genitive are in a place of accusative as a circumstantial qualifier, i.e., being from the affirmation of the beliefs of Islam. And the same applies in similar examples. Then some people denied the coming of 'min' for clarifying the genus, and according to them it is for partitive, as is not hidden. (Muhammad Ali)
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe on the use of the particle 'min' in the matn. The commentator explains that 'min' in the phrase is for clarifying the genus (bayān al-jins). He notes that although 'min' often appears after words like 'mā' and 'mahmā', as in Quranic examples such as 'Mā nansakh min āya' (What verse We abrogate) and 'Mahmā ta'tinā bihi min āya' (Whatever sign you bring us), it can also occur after other words. He gives the Quranic example 'Fajtanibū l-rijsa mina l-awthān' (So avoid the abomination of idols), where 'min' specifies the genus of abomination. He further states that the phrase 'min taqrīr ʿaqāʾid al-Islām' is in the accusative case as a circumstantial qualifier (ḥāl). Finally, he notes that some scholars denied that 'min' can be for clarifying the genus, insisting it must be partitive (tabʿīḍ). This passage helps the reader correctly parse the particle's function.

Key Terms
بيان الجنس
حال
من

Checkpoint

A) Partitive (tabʿīḍ)
B) Generic specification (bayān al-jins)
C) Causal (sababiyya)
D) Temporal (zamāniyya)

Key Takeaway
The particle 'min' can function to specify the genus, and recognizing this is essential for accurate grammatical analysis of Islamic texts.

Classifying Semantic Relations in Idāfa
Author classifies the types of idafa based on semantic relation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the semantic relation between the two terms of an idāfa construction as possession, containment, or impossible based on the four-relation rule.

Core Idea
Idāfa is not just possession; its meaning depends on the logical relation between the two terms.

In Arabic, the idāfa (possessive/genitive construction) often expresses ownership, but a closer look reveals a rich semantic structure. The majority of scholars (jumhūr) hold that the semantic idāfa is primarily in the meaning of lām (possession) and occasionally in the meaning of fī (containment). This lesson unpacks the rule (ḍābiṭ) that governs which meaning applies: the two terms must be related by one of four logical relations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two terms
In any idāfa construction, locate the first term (muḍāf) and the second term (muḍāf ilayhi). For example, in 'ṣalāt al-masjid', 'ṣalāt' is muḍāf and 'al-masjid' is muḍāf ilayhi.
2
Determine the logical relation
Check if the two terms are equal, disparate, absolutely general, or general from one aspect. The rule states that idāfa is impossible in cases of equality and disparity without a relation, and when the added-to is more general absolutely.
3
Check for containment
If the relation exists and is containment (the second term is a container for the first, time or place), the idāfa is in the meaning of 'fī' (in). Example: 'ṣalāt al-masjid' – the mosque contains the prayer.
4
Otherwise, possession or other relations
If the relation exists but is not containment, the idāfa is in the meaning of 'lām' (possession), covering ownership, part-whole, kinship, etc. Example: 'thawb Zayd' – the garment of Zayd (ownership).
5
Identify impossible cases
Equality (e.g., two identical terms), disparity without any relation, and absolute generality of the second term over the first make idāfa impossible unless reinterpreted.
The passage also mentions 'generality from one aspect' but does not elaborate; it is likely a case where idāfa is possible but not covered here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۱۱) قوله والاضافة في عقايد الاسلام بيانية : اعلم ان المشهور عند الجمهور ان الاضافة المعنوية تكون على معنى اللام باكثرية وعلى معنى فى بقلة والضابط : ان الشيئين اللذين يعتبر بينهما الاضافة لابد و ان يتحقق بينهما احدى النسب الاربع اما التساوى او التباين أو العموم المطلق أو العموم من وجه . فعلى الأول يمتنع الاضافة الابتأويل يلحقه بالثلاثة الآخر. و على الثانى اما ان يكون بينهما نسبة واضافة ام لا و على الثانى يمتنع الاضافة ايضاً وعلى الأول ان كانت النسبة هى الظرفية بان يكون المضاف اليه ظرفاً للمضاف فالاضافة بمعنى (في» سواء كان ظرف زمان نحو: «مكر الليل» و «تربص أربعة اشهر او ظرف مكان نحو يا صاحبي السجن» و «صلوة المسجد و الا فيمعنى اللام سواء كان المضاف ظرفاً للمضاف اليه ـ مسجد الصلوة» و «منبر الوعظ » او جزء منه كه ید «زید» او كجزء» که «کلام «زید» او ملكاً له كـ ثوب زيد وعبده» او كملك که «جل الفرس او ان يتحقق بينهما القرابة كـ «ابی زید و ابنه وعمه وخاله» وغير ذلك مما لانهاية له. و على الثالث ان كان المضاف اليه اعم و المضاف اخص که احد اليوم» مثلاً فالأضافة ممتنعة
(111) His words 'and the idafa in the beliefs of Islam is explanatory': Know that the well-known view among the majority is that the semantic idafa is mostly in the meaning of lām (possession) and rarely in the meaning of fī (in). The rule is: the two things between which idafa is considered must have one of the four relations: either equality, disparity, absolute generality, or generality from one aspect. On the first (equality), idafa is impossible except by interpretation that attaches it to the other three. On the second (disparity), either there is a relationship and idafa between them or not; on the second, idafa is also impossible. On the first (now referring back to the case of relation existing), if the relation is of containment (ẓarfiyya) such that the second term is a container for the first, then the idafa is in the meaning of 'fī', whether it is a container of time like 'the plot of the night' and 'a postponement of four months' or a container of place like 'O two companions of the prison' and 'the prayer of the mosque'. Otherwise it is in the meaning of 'lām', whether the added is a container for the added-to like 'mosque of prayer' and 'pulpit of preaching', or a part of it like 'hand of Zayd', or like a part like 'speech of Zayd', or a possession of his like 'garment of Zayd' and 'his slave', or like possession like 'horse's saddle', or if there is kinship between them like 'father of Zayd', 'his son', 'his uncle', and 'his maternal uncle', and other things without end. On the third (absolute generality of the added-to over the added), if the added-to is more general and the added is more specific, like 'one of the days' for example, then idafa is impossible.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the types of idāfa (possessive/genitive construction) in Arabic. The author begins by stating that the well-known view is that semantic idāfa is mostly in the meaning of lām (possession) and rarely in the meaning of fī (containment). He then provides a rule: the two terms involved must have one of four relations: equality (tasāwī), disparity (tabāyun), absolute generality (ʿumūm muṭlaq), or generality from one aspect (ʿumūm min wajh). He then details each case:
- Equality: idāfa is impossible unless reinterpreted.
- Disparity: if there is no relation, idāfa is impossible; if there is a relation, then if it is containment, idāfa is in the meaning of 'fī' (time or place examples), otherwise it is in the meaning of 'lām' (including possession, part-whole, kinship, etc.).
- Absolute generality (added-to general, added specific): idāfa is impossible.
- Generality from one aspect: (not elaborated here).

This classification helps in understanding the semantic relation in idāfa constructions, especially in the phrase 'iḍāfa fī ʿaqāʾid al-islām', which is said to be explanatory (bayāniyya).

Key Terms
إضافة معنوية
اللام
في

B) Containment (fī) because the mosque contains the prayer
C) Impossible because equality
D) Absolute generality

Key Takeaway
The meaning of idāfa—possession (lām) or containment (fī)—is determined by the logical relation between the two terms, with a four-relation rule governing possibility.

Distinguishing 'Adam I'tibar from I'tibar al-'Adam
Clarifies that not considering something is not considering its non-existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between 'not considering a thing' and 'considering its non-existence' and explain why conflating them leads to invalid objections in Islamic theological discourse.

Core Idea
Not considering something is not the same as considering it non-existent.

In Islamic jurisprudence and theology, precise distinctions are crucial. A common error is to equate 'not considering' a ruling or belief with 'considering it absent'. This lesson unpacks that distinction as presented in a hashya on Qanun al-Islam, showing how conflating them can lead to false accusations of disbelief.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection being addressed
The objection claims that if a sage holds a belief contrary to the sharia, he would be an unbeliever. The author responds by clarifying the logical status of 'not considering'.
The objection relies on equating lack of consideration with affirming the opposite.
2
Isolate the key distinction
The author states: 'For not considering a thing is not considering its non-existence.' This is the central logical point: 'adam i'tibar (absence of consideration) is not equivalent to i'tibar al-'adam (consideration of absence).
This aligns with logical principles in usul al-fiqh regarding default states.
3
Apply the distinction to the objection
If a sage does not consider a certain ruling, that does not mean he considers the ruling false or non-existent. Thus, the objection that he is an unbeliever is invalid.
The author's refutation hinges on this logical nuance.
4
Recognize the broader import in Islamic sciences
This distinction appears often in debates about takfir (declaring someone an unbeliever) and in interpreting ambiguous statements. It protects against hasty judgments.
Similar distinctions are used in usul al-fiqh when discussing the absence of evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قانون الإسلام لا انه يعتبر ان تكون على خلافه حتى يرد انه يلزم كون الحكيم المعتقد للمحكمة كافراً غير مسلم لكون اعتقاده على خلاف الشريعة المطهرة الطاهرة فان عدم اعتبار الشيء ليس باعتبار لعدمه كما هو ظاهر. (محمد علی)
The rule of Islam [is] that it is not considered that it be contrary to it, so that it might be objected that it entails that the sage who believes in the judgment is an unbeliever, not a Muslim, because his belief is contrary to the pure and holy sharia. For not considering a thing is not considering its non-existence, as is apparent. (Muhammad Ali)
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation of an objection. The author addresses a hypothetical objection: if a sage holds a belief contrary to the sharia, he would be an unbeliever. The author clarifies that merely not considering something (i.e., not taking it into account) does not constitute considering its non-existence. The absence of consideration is not the same as a positive judgment of absence. Therefore, the objection is invalid. This is a typical logical and theological nuance found in hashya literature.

Key Terms
قانون الإسلام
عدم اعتبار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Not considering something is a neutral act, not a positive judgment of its non-existence.

Grammatical Factor in Co-ordination
Discusses different opinions on the grammatical factor governing the co-ordinated word.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four opinions on the grammatical factor in co-ordination and explain why the majority view is preferred.

Core Idea
The factor of the co-ordinated word is that of the first word, transmitted via the particle.

In Arabic grammar, the co-ordinated word (al-ma'tuf) receives its case ending from a 'factor' (al-'amil). Scholars debated what that factor is. This lesson unpacks the four views and the reasoning behind the dominant position, as presented in a classical hashia.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
The passage asks: what grammatical factor (عامل) governs the case ending of the co-ordinated word (المعطوف)? Recognize that this is a foundational question in Arabic syntax.
2
List the four opinions
The text states: (1) the factor is the same as the factor of the first word, via the particle (majority); (2) the particle itself; (3) an implied factor after the conjunction; (4) the superordinate word (المتبوع). Find each opinion in the Arabic.
3
Assess the author's stance
The author declares the first opinion 'the correct one' (وهو الصحيح). Note that he also mentions apparent evidence for the fourth view but does not accept it.
4
Analyze the additional interpretation
The author discusses a possible co-ordination of a word to 'al-tahrir', citing al-Dawani. Then he critiques that interpretation as verbally close but conceptually inappropriate, which is why the original commentator (al-muhashi) ignored it.
This shows careful evaluation of textual-corpus versus meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الظاهر من كلامه ان العامل فى المعطوف هو عامل المعطوف عليه بواسطة الحرف كما عليه الجمهور وهو الصحيح. وذهب بعضهم الى ان العامل هو الحرف وقال بعضهم : ان العامل مقدر بعد العاطف وقال بعضهم لو قيل العامل فى التابع هو المتبوع لكان لهم شواهد و يحتمل ان يكون معطوفاً على التحرير (كما قال به الفاضل الدوانى والمعنى هذا غاية تهذيب الكلام فى تقريب المقاصد ای : سوق الدليل على وجه يستلزم المطلوب. هكذا قيل. وفيه انه و ان كان بحسب اللفظ اقرب الا أنه ليس بحسب المعنى أنسب كما لا يخفى على من له فكر اصوب وذهن ارهب ولذا لم يتعرض له المحشى. (عبد الرحيم)
It is apparent from his statement that the factor in the co-ordinated [word] is the factor of the word it is co-ordinated to, by means of the particle, as held by the majority and it is correct. Some went to the factor being the particle, and some said the factor is implied after the co-ordinating conjunction, and some said if it were said that the factor in the subordinate is the superordinate, they would have evidence. And it is possible that it is co-ordinated to 'al-tahrir' as stated by al-Fadil al-Dawani, and the meaning is: this is the ultimate refinement of speech in approximating the intentions, i.e., presenting the proof in a way that entails the desired. Thus it is said. And in it [there is that] although it is closer verbally, it is not more appropriate in meaning, as is not hidden from one who has sounder thought and more awe-inspiring mind, and therefore the commentator did not address it. (Abd al-Rahim)
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the grammatical rule for co-ordination ('atf). The author states the majority view: the grammatical factor governing the co-ordinated word is the same factor that governs the word it is co-ordinated to, conveyed via the co-ordinating particle. He then lists other opinions: some say the particle itself is the factor, some say an implied factor after the conjunction, and some suggest that the factor could be the superordinate word. The author then shifts to a possible interpretation of a phrase in the text, connecting it to the concept of 'ultimate refinement of speech' as presenting proof that entails the conclusion. He concludes that while this interpretation is verbally closer, it is not more appropriate in meaning, so the commentator ignored it.

Key Terms
العامل (al-'amil): The grammatical factor that governs the case ending of a word.
المعطوف (al-ma'tuf): The co-ordinated word in a grammatical co-ordination structure.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The particle itself is the factor.
B) The factor is implied after the conjunction.
C) The factor of the co-ordinated word is the same as the factor of the first word, transmitted via the particle.
D) The superordinate word is the factor.

Key Takeaway
The majority view in Arabic grammar is that the factor governing the co-ordinated word is the same as the factor governing the word it is co-ordinated to, conveyed through the co-ordinating particle.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

In the verse {فَأَمَّا الْيَتِيمَ فَلَا تَقْهَرْ وَأَمَّا السَّائِلَ فَلَا تَنْهَرْ} (Ad-Duha 9-10), identify the factor governing the accusative case of 'السائل' and explain how co-ordination works here using the majority view.

Parsing Definitional Phrases in Logic
Explains grammatical analysis of a definitional phrase.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to parse the grammatical structure of a definitional phrase in a logical text and explain the two possible readings of 'ghayat taqrib al-maram'.

Core Idea
Grammatical parsing of a definition reveals its intended logical force.

In logical commentaries, authors often pause to clarify the grammar of a key phrase. This lesson examines such a pause: the analysis of 'ghayat taqrib al-maram' (the ultimate approximation of the intended meaning) as it functions in a definition. Understanding this parsing helps you see how definitions can be understood literally or hyperbolically.

Guided Path
1
Identify the phrase under analysis
Find the phrase 'ghayat taqrib al-maram' in the Arabic. It is being parsed as the predicate of 'hadha' (this).
2
Understand the first reading: hyperbole
The first possibility treats the verbal noun 'ghayat' as an exaggerated predicate, like saying 'Zayd is justice' where the verbal noun substitutes for the person. Here, 'hadha' (this) is said to be the ultimate approximation itself.
This is called 'mubalaghah' in Arabic rhetoric.
3
Understand the second reading: absolute object substitution
The second reading assumes the actual predicate is deleted, and 'ghayat taqrib al-maram' is an absolute object (maf'ul mutlaq) that has been elevated to predicate status, acquiring nominative case. The implied meaning is 'this speech is a maximally approximating thing'.
This reading requires reconstructing an active participle like 'muqarrib'.
4
Evaluate the preferred reading
The author prefers the active participle 'muqarrib' (as stated by al-Fadil al-Dawani) over the passive 'muqarrab', though the latter is permissible with some stretch. Note how grammatical choice affects meaning.
Active participle emphasizes the action, passive emphasizes the object.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله و الحمل اى حمل قوله غاية تقريب المرام على كلمة اسم الاشارة هذا اما على طريقة المبالغة كما يقال فى حمل المصادر على الذوات نحو زيد «عدل او ان خبر المبتداء محذوف و غاية تقريب» «المرام» مفعول مطلق اقيم مقامه فاعطى حكمه وهو الرفع على الخبرية بعد ما كان منصوباً على المفعولية والتقدير: هذا الكلام مقرب غاية التقريب وقد تقدم مثله في قوله: فهذا غاية تهذيب الكلام». (التقريب ص ۱۱) لا يخفى ان الاولى ان يقرء «مقرب» بصبغة اسم الفاعل كما صرح به الفاضل الدواني و يجوز على بعد صيغة المفعول ايضاً. (محمد على)
His statement: 'and the predicate' i.e., predication of his statement 'ghayat taqrib al-maram' to the demonstrative pronoun 'hadha' either in the manner of exaggeration, as it is said in predicating verbal nouns to entities like 'Zayd [is] justice', or [it is] that the predicate of the subject is deleted and 'ghayat taqrib al-maram' is an absolute object that was substituted for it and given its rule, which is nominative as predicate after it had been accusative as object, and the estimation: 'this speech is a maximally approximating thing', and an example of that has preceded in his statement 'fahadha ghayat tahdhib al-kalam'. (al-Taqrib p. 11) It is not hidden that it is preferable to read 'muqarrib' in the form of the active participle, as stated by al-Fadil al-Dawani, and it is permissible with some distance the form of the passive participle also. (Muhammad Ali)
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage is a grammatical analysis of the phrase 'ghayat taqrib al-maram' (the ultimate approximation of the intended meaning) as it is used in a definition. The author explains two possibilities for how this phrase functions as a predicate for 'hadha' (this). The first is that it is an exaggerated attribution, like saying 'Zayd is justice' where the verbal noun is used hyperbolically. The second is that the actual predicate is deleted and the phrase is an absolute object that takes its place, acquiring its nominative case. The author prefers reading 'muqarrib' (active participle) rather than 'muqarrab' (passive participle), following al-Dawani, though both are possible. This kind of parsing is common in logical works to clarify the meaning of definitions.

Key Terms
غاية تقريب المرام
مفعول مطلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because it is more common
B) Because it avoids ambiguity
C) Because al-Fadil al-Dawani stated that reading
D) Because the passive participle is grammatically incorrect

Key Takeaway
Grammatical parsing of definitional phrases in logic reveals whether a definition is literal or hyperbolic, affecting its logical interpretation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Understanding 'Min' as Bayan al-Jins
Discusses the function of the particle 'min' as bayan al-jins (explication of genus).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when the particle 'min' functions as bayan al-jins and distinguish it from partitivity in Quranic verses.

Core Idea
The particle 'min' can explicate the genus, not just indicate partitivity.

The Arabic particle 'min' is often understood as indicating partitivity (some, part of). However, it can also function as 'min bayan al-jins', explicating the genus or category of something. This distinction is crucial for correctly interpreting Quranic verses and logical definitions. In this lesson, we will explore this function and its significance.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the context
Observe that 'min' often appears after the interrogatives 'ma' and 'mahma', as in 'ma nansakh min ayat' (whatever verse We abrogate). In such constructions, it typically explicates the genus of the thing in question.
These are common patterns, but not exclusive.
2
Examine the given verse
Look at the verse 'fajtanibu al-rijsa min al-awthan' (avoid the filth of idols). Here, 'min' connects 'al-rijs' (filth) with 'al-awthan' (idols), indicating that the filth is of the genus of idols, not just a part of them.
This is a clear example of 'min bayan al-jins'.
3
Understand the scholarly debate
Some scholars deny that 'min' ever functions as bayan al-jins, insisting it always indicates partitivity. Consider how this would change the meaning of the verse and why the author argues against it.
The author sides with the majority that bayan al-jins is a valid function.
4
Apply to other contexts
Practice by identifying whether 'min' in a new Quranic or logical phrase is partitive or explicative. Ask: Does it indicate a subset or does it specify the genus?
This skill is essential for precise interpretation in tafsir and usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يعنى ان كلمة «من» لبيان الجنس فان هذه و ان كان اكثر وقوعها بعدما و مهما لكثرة ابها مهما نحو: «ما ننسخ من آية ...» ، «مهما تأتنا به من آية» لكنها قدييجي بعد غير هما ايضاً قال تعالى: «فاجتنبوا الرجس من الاوثان ثم هى و مخفوضها في محل النصب على الحالية اى كائناً من تقرير عقايد الاسلام وكذا الحال فى امثال ذلك. ثم ان قوماً انكر مجى ( من البيان الجنس وعليه فهى للتبعيض كما لا يخفى. (محمد على)
He means that the word 'min' is for explicating the genus, for although it occurs mostly after 'ma' and 'mahma' due to their abundance, as in 'ma nansakh min ayat...' and 'mahma ta'tina bihi min ayat', it also comes after other than them. Almighty said: 'fajtanibu al-rijsa min al-awthan' then it and its genitive are in the accusative position as a circumstantial accusative, i.e., being from the determination of the beliefs of Islam, and likewise in similar instances. Then some people denied the occurrence of 'min' for explication of genus, and according to them it is for partitivity, as is not hidden. (Muhammad Ali)
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage explains that the particle 'min' can function as 'li bayan al-jins' (for explication of the genus). The author notes that although it often appears after interrogatives like 'ma' and 'mahma', it also occurs elsewhere, citing the Quranic verse 'fajtanibu al-rijsa min al-awthan' (avoid the filth of idols). Here, 'min' explicates the genus of what to avoid. The author then mentions that some scholars deny this usage, insisting that 'min' always indicates partitivity (al-tab'id). This is a grammatical nuance that affects the interpretation of definitions in logical texts, as the same word can indicate inclusion or partiality.

للتبعيض

Key Takeaway
The particle 'min' has multiple functions; recognizing 'min bayan al-jins' is crucial for accurate interpretation of definitions in Islamic texts.

Commentary Notes
intermediate
7 min
Determining the Type of Iḍāfa in Definitions
Author discusses the meaning of iḍāfa in the definition of Islam and critiques a proposed alternative interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether an iḍāfa in a definition is lāmiyya, miniyya, or bayāniyya, and evaluate whether a proposed interpretation violates scholarly consensus.

Core Idea
The type of iḍāfa in a definition reveals whether the definiens is a possession or an explanation.

In defining terms like 'Islam', the grammatical relationship between the definiendum and definiens matters. The author critiques a commentator's proposal that the iḍāfa is explanatory, showing how grammatical rules from Arabic grammar, applied in logic, guide correct definition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the terms in the iḍāfa
Find the two nouns in the construct state: the first (muḍāf) and the second (muḍāf ilayh). In 'Islam ʿibāratun ʿan al-iʿtiqādāt', the iḍāfa is between 'Islam' and 'beliefs'.
2
Determine the relationship of generality
Check whether the muḍāf is more general or more specific than the muḍāf ilayh. The text says Islam is absolute generality relative to beliefs (Islam includes beliefs and actions), so beliefs are more specific.
3
Apply the rule for iḍāfa type
If the muḍāf ilayh is more specific (a kind of the muḍāf), the iḍāfa is lāmiyya (possessive). If the muḍāf ilayh is an origin (aṣl) for the muḍāf, it is miniyya (partitive). If it is explanatory (apposition), it is bayāniyya.
Examples: 'shajar al-arāk' (arak tree) is lāmiyya; 'khātam ḥadīd' (ring of iron) is miniyya.
4
Evaluate the proposed alternative
The commentator suggested bayāniyya, but the author argues this violates the consensus of scholars because the relationship is not apposition but specification. Therefore, the iḍāfa must be lāmiyya.
The author uses the rule that when the muḍāf ilayh is more specific and not an origin, iḍāfa is lāmiyya only.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في مقدمة الكتاب الابتأويل، والا فهى بمعنى اللام كـ «يوم الاحد» و «علم الفقه» و «شجر الاراك». و على الرابع فان كان المضاف اليه اصلاً للمضاف فالاضافة بمعنى من والا فبمعنى اللام ايضاً. فإذا تبين هذا فاعلم انه اذا كان الاسلام عبارة عن نفس الاعتقادات يكون بينه وبين العقايد عموم مطلقا والمضاف اليه اخص وقد عرفت ان الاضافة ح تكون بمعنى اللام لاغير وكان ما ذكره المحشى مبنى على ما افاده بعض المحققين من ان الانسب بحسب المعنى ان تكون الاضافة ح بيانية و اظهار «من» (الجارة) فيها خال عن التكلف. ولا يخفى ان هذا خرق لإجماعهم. (میرزا محمد علی)
In the introduction of the book: the beginning, and it is with the meaning of the lām, like 'the day of Sunday', 'the science of jurisprudence', and 'the arak tree'. And according to the fourth [case]: if the annexed is an origin for the annexer, then the iḍāfa is with the meaning of 'min'; otherwise it is with the meaning of lām as well. So when this is clear, know that if Islam is an expression of the beliefs themselves, then between it and the beliefs there is absolute generality, and the annexed is more specific. And you have known that the iḍāfa here is only with the meaning of lām. And what the commentator (al-muḥashshī) mentioned is based on what some investigators said: that the most appropriate in terms of meaning is that the iḍāfa here is explanatory (bayāniyya), and to express 'min' (the preposition) in it is free of affectation. And it is not hidden that this violates their consensus. (Mīrzā Muḥammad ʿAlī)
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of a prior commentator's view on the iḍāfa in the phrase 'Islam is the beliefs'. The author, Mīrzā Muḥammad ʿAlī, explains the rules of iḍāfa: when the annexed is a specification, the iḍāfa is lāmiyya (possessive), but if the annexed is an origin, it is miniyya (partitive). In the case of 'Islam' and 'beliefs', since 'Islam' is more general and 'beliefs' more specific, the iḍāfa must be lāmiyya. He refutes the suggestion that it is bayāniyya (explanatory), arguing that this violates the consensus of scholars. The examples given are from Islamic sciences: 'science of fiqh', 'arak tree' (used for miswak), etc.

Key Terms
إضافة
اللام
بيانية

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Lām (possessive)
B) Min (partitive)
C) Bayāniyya (explanatory)
D) It is not specified

Key Takeaway
The correct identification of iḍāfa type in a definition is crucial for precision; a mistaken iḍāfa can distort the meaning and violate scholarly consensus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the definition of 'ṣawm' as 'imtināʿ ʿan al-mufṭirāt' (abstinence from breaking things). Determine whether the iḍāfa is lāmiyya or miniyya, and justify using the rules from the passage.
?
The definition of 'īmān' is often given as 'taṣdīq bi al-qalb' (assent by the heart). Analyze the iḍāfa in this definition: would it be lāmiyya, miniyya, or bayāniyya? Explain your reasoning.
